  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c1d9a913-55e6-48f4-a2a7-b68d91556ee9'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer6193225668792281093">Okay, listen up, girls, because this book has some major important life advice here:<br/><br/>If you happen to get kidnapped and abused by a heroin addict when you are 14 yrs old, and then run into him when you are 20, only to have him abuse you again. Then, he kicks his heroin addiction, yet still abuses you just a couple of more times, only to later reveal that he didn't enjoy it as much because he now loves you. That's totally fine. You should totally marry that guy because he's sorry.<br/><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/images/oh%20no%20she%20didn%27t' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81635051?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/2972467-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who can form their own opinion</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2972467-andrea?shelf=to-be-published">to-be-published</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer81635051&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81635051" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13165204826339618337">Review of ‘Spy Glass’ Opal Cowan #3<br/><br/>By Maria V. Snyder. (Thanks Net Galley for the ARC.)<br/>To be Published September 17th 2010 by Mira Books<br/><br/>I wrote this review almost 6 years ago and I still agree with what I originally wrote. <br/><br/>The overall story was fine. It was a huge bonus to see Yelena, Janko, Ari, Iris and Valek again. But where was Zitora? She was a huge part of the last two books, but was absent from this one, and she seemed to have her own story to fulfil at the end of ‘Sea Glass’. Perhaps a n</span>
  <span id="freeText13165204826339618337" style="display:none">Review of ‘Spy Glass’ Opal Cowan #3<br /><br />By Maria V. Snyder. (Thanks Net Galley for the ARC.)<br />To be Published September 17th 2010 by Mira Books<br /><br />I wrote this review almost 6 years ago and I still agree with what I originally wrote. <br /><br />The overall story was fine. It was a huge bonus to see Yelena, Janko, Ari, Iris and Valek again. But where was Zitora? She was a huge part of the last two books, but was absent from this one, and she seemed to have her own story to fulfil at the end of ‘Sea Glass’. Perhaps a new series? That would be well worth the wait.<br /><br />Yelena, Janko, Ari, Iris and Valek were very pleasant to read again and they added a lot to the skittish plot and weak character developments.<br />Now to the part of the story that enraged me to the point that it was difficult to finish the book. If you do not want spoilers, than please do not read any more. <br /> <br />Opal and her overall relationship choice. Wow, it is a little strange that a book which is undoubtedly read by younger people would have one of the core characters enter into a relationship with the man who, and this is a quote from the book “A year and a half ago he had kidnapped and tortured me”. This relationship was also started when she was in a relationship with someone else. There has been an attempt to explain this away with the blood magic addiction. Seriously? <br /><br />Devlin also seems to be present as some kind of ‘Valek’ type replacement. Sadly, it did not work. Dislike for him still lingered heavily from the previous books. It is also one of the most distractingly annoying aspects of this book; being asked to accept a character that deceived, kidnapped, and tortured (also possibly raped) the main person and the excuses offered to explain why, were not very adequate. I also believe it is not the best idea to gloss over such important issues.<br /> <br />Lastly, the portrayal of some of the characters was one of the most distracing aspects. One of the worst off was Kade, it seemed like he was treated as a means to an end, and as such, was reduced to a meek doorstep that was hardly present in the story at all. Perhaps he was off with Zitora? It is a shame that one of the most recognisable people from the previous two books, who the readers have indentified strongly with Opal, was reduced to this. <br /><br />Spending two books setting this charcter up, only to tear them down almost feels like a waste of time. The feeling that comes from reading cover–to-cover is that there was no real idea where his story was going, and that it was more a seat-of-your-pants story. Again, perhaps Kade will get his own spin off series? <br /><br />One of the better things in this book was the twist with the black diamonds. It would seem there is another Glass Wizard! Quinn was an awesome person to read, and seemed to be a new addition to Opals collection of people. Dealing with the problems within the compound was also a good way to pick up the pace of the storyline and bring the interest back to the wider story. Some twists and turns in the book were also a well played, even if you guessed what would happen.<br /><br />‘Spy Glass’ seems to have good bits, and not so good bits... However, it is still enjoyable if you can put these issues to the side. * <b>Almost 6 years later and I now disagree with this. It was not enjoyable, and this story bothers me to this day</b>.<br /><br />Don't bother reading this book<br /><br /><br />THIS IS MY OPINION! I enjoyed the other aspects of the book, however<br />I will admit it is hard to recommend a book that contains certain events that are against my morals.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13165204826339618337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_92520228" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92520228" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1121573-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410285945p2/1121573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92520228?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/1121573-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780778328476" href="/book/show/7698740-spy-glass">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1121573-samantha?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1121573-samantha?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer92520228&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92520228" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13719804013557698708">****SPOILERS FOR THE PREVIOUS STORIES*****<br/><br/><br/>No, no, no. This one didn't work for me on sooo many different levels, which is disappointing. It's only because I am a fan of this author's other stories that I have trudged on, hoping for a shift.<br/><br/>First there's the totality of the character that is Devlen. He has tortured (both mentally and physically) Opal in the past and now it's been put off to something he did because of blood magic. Let's just insert a convenient 'soul-reader' to instantly say that</span>
  <span id="freeText13719804013557698708" style="display:none">****SPOILERS FOR THE PREVIOUS STORIES*****<br /><br /><br />No, no, no. This one didn't work for me on sooo many different levels, which is disappointing. It's only because I am a fan of this author's other stories that I have trudged on, hoping for a shift.<br /><br />First there's the totality of the character that is Devlen. He has tortured (both mentally and physically) Opal in the past and now it's been put off to something he did because of blood magic. Let's just insert a convenient 'soul-reader' to instantly say that a certain character is no longer 'bad' and hello, easy-street! I don't care what kind of magical stupor you're under that would cause bad behavior, memories of torture alone would never allow me to interact with that person. Never ever, ever, seriously Ever. I've seen the various reviews/comments here on Goodreads on whether Opal was raped by Devlen and it's fine if you don't think so call it what you want. Of course in reality we're never going to have people conveniently switching souls and then pretending to be your significant other. For me the fact is, Opal thought she was with Ulrick, and that she consented to sex is secondary to the fact that <u>he wasn't Ulrick</u>. It doesn't matter if she enjoyed being with Delven-in-a-Ulrick-suit, she didn't know it was really the man who inhabited her worst nightmares and caused a lot of her feelings of inadequacy. Don't be too surprised here, but even creeps can act nice to their victims to get the results they want. I know, crazy right? If I were Opal I would have felt totally violated, my trust in my own judgement would have been in shambles…sound like Opal at all? Maybe I should have stopped reading after Opal comments on Yelena's 'readings' on Devlen, because obviously it's enough to leave me disgusted.<br /><br />Yet I continued on because I thought there would be a story in here somewhere. A story that showed Opal coming into her own person. Yet throughout most of this story that is still painfully absent as we are forced to accompany her through a sham of a plot to obtain her missing blood. And even though that's the focus of the plot, it meanders here and there with no direction other than to insert convenient events to recollect upon later in the story. It felt like I was reading something completely different by last third of the book and not in a good way.<br /><br />Then there's the generally unenjoyable dialogue and childish, petty characters across the board. These are Snyder's characters and I've liked them in the past (especially in Yelena's series), but this time even though they had the same names and were supposed to be the same people, some didn't sound like themselves. They seemed out of character to me, especially Valek in this one, but then again I'm only one reader and I'm sure some will be fine with it. <br /><br />So anyway in the interest of finding a balance between brevity (fail) and getting this stuff off my chest, I'm ending it here. I wouldn't read anymore books about Opal if you paid me and I hope that if Snyder continues to write in this world it will not result in the overwhelming disappointment I have had in this series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13719804013557698708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82408795" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82408795" />
    <a title="Chichipio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1870710-chichipio"><img alt="Chichipio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308898844p2/1870710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82408795?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chichipio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chichipio" href="/user/show/1870710-chichipio">Chichipio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780778328476" href="/book/show/7698740-spy-glass">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1870710-chichipio?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82408795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2544701940867615005">Phew! I'm done with Maria V. Snyder and her series. That tiny part of me that suffers OCD can finally be put to sleep.<br/><br/>When I first read Poison Study, I thought Snyder's writing was terrific. Tight plot where things really made sense and excellent characters—smart, funny and relatable. Then, slowly but surely, the quality dropped. Books #2 and #3 in the Study series were pretty meh. I still liked them but it was mostly because of some of the characters having made such a good first impression pre</span>
  <span id="freeText2544701940867615005" style="display:none">Phew! I'm done with Maria V. Snyder and her series. That tiny part of me that suffers OCD can finally be put to sleep.<br /><br />When I first read Poison Study, I thought Snyder's writing was terrific. Tight plot where things really made sense and excellent characters—smart, funny and relatable. Then, slowly but surely, the quality dropped. Books #2 and #3 in the Study series were pretty meh. I still liked them but it was mostly because of some of the characters having made such a good first impression previously. The fact that I didn't like almost any of the new characters introduced after the first book should have been all the warning I needed not to start a new series. But, of course, where's the fun in heeding good advice?<br /><br />So I started the Glass series still riding the positive feelings left by that first book. Big mistake. Even with that injection of optimism, I still didn't like Opal, Zitora and the whole group of male protagonists. However, the second book was already out, so I just kept going on autopilot and read it. That only made me dislike these characters more. There are a few exceptions here and there, of course, but not nearly enough to make up for all the rest. Had this book been out back then, I would have read it right away, if only to find out how things turned out. But this wasn't published until several months later. By that time, I had lost any desire of reading this. Every now and then, however, a stray thought would cross my mind along the lines of "I wonder if she ever did manage to get her magic back" or "will she end up with the idiot without any personality or the idiot who tortured her at several different moments in her life?" In the end, curiosity won over common sense and I decided to give it a try. Well, let's just say that curiosity sucks.<br /><br />Everything that bothered me before made an appearance this time as well. I don't even feel like going into a detailed account of all that I found wrong here. I know I'm probably being unfair, but going against my better judgment and suffering the consequences for it, makes me grouchy.<br /><br />For what it's worth, let me point you to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91501508" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Penny's review</a>. She manages to give a quick, funny rundown of the series and this book in particular, pointing out its flaws without devolving into an angry troll—unlike me, If I try to do the same.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2544701940867615005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_91501508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91501508" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/679025-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323234939p2/679025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91501508?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/679025-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=guilty-pleasures">guilty-pleasures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=wizardry">wizardry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=grrrl-power">grrrl-power</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91501508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1165786223298390761">Quick review: Opal Cowan, glassmaker, "one trick wonder" and victim extraordinaire, spends the majority of the first two Glass books helping others, rehashing traumatic experiences, sparring or traveling from one place to another. <br/><br/>At practically every single village she visits, and sometimes in the middle of nowhere, she's beaten, or falsely imprisoned, or tortured, or kidnapped. The girl just can't catch a break--people want to steal her magic, or, you know, just want her to die. But resourcefu</span>
  <span id="freeText1165786223298390761" style="display:none">Quick review: Opal Cowan, glassmaker, "one trick wonder" and victim extraordinaire, spends the majority of the first two Glass books helping others, rehashing traumatic experiences, sparring or traveling from one place to another. <br /><br />At practically every single village she visits, and sometimes in the middle of nowhere, she's beaten, or falsely imprisoned, or tortured, or kidnapped. The girl just can't catch a break--people want to steal her magic, or, you know, just want her to die. But resourceful girl that she is, Opal always manages to get out of sticky situations, somehow. <br /><br />Along the way she picks up a couple of suitors: Kade, a powerful stormdancer with the personality of a dead fish and a never ending supply of weather analogies; Ulrick, a handsome, extremely overprotective glassmaker who lacks confidence, integrity, and any significant amount of magic; and Devlin, a good-looking former blood magic addict, *whispers* who used to torture Opal, and, switched souls with a (very willing) Ulrick in order to seduce Opal, *whisper mumbling* and then kidnap and torture her further. And then fall in love with her. And then save her life. And save her friends lives. And then apologize to Opal for all the horrid things he did to her. And finally turn himself into the authorities, after giving Opal a gift. And a kiss. (BTW, at some point Opal drains Devlin of all his magic. I just can't remember when).<br /><br />All caught up now? Good. <br /><br />In Spy Glass, the final installment in the Glass series, Opal is mourning the loss of her magic, which she sacrificed in order to save the day at the end of Sea Glass. Ever since then she hasn't been the same, feels as though she's lost her whole identity. Instead of accepting a lifetime without magic, Opal decides she's going to get it back. <br /><br />At one point, Opal pays Devlin a visit in prison in order to question him about blood magic, and if he knows if any of the blood taken from her, before she lost her magic, is preserved and hidden somewhere. While meeting with the newly reformed Devlin, Opal discovers she has extremely mixed feelings about him. On one hand, she know she can't trust him, he still terrifies her. And on the other, she feels drawn to him because he too has been stripped of all his magic. He understands what she's going through when no one else does. Also, he's changed so much, is humble and repentant. <br /><br />On top of everything, Opal is trying to decide if she wants to spend the rest of her life with Kade, the storm dancer. <br /><br />Lots of drama ensues. <br /><br />Sounds like a great series, right? ;) Okay, so I'm not being completely fair, I made it sound so much worse then it actually is. It's not that bad. Although it's not that good either. That being said, I still like Maria V. Snyder's Glass series. Yeah, I like it. Why? I can't say why. Really, I can't. <br /><br />Overall the series was satisfying in a way I just can't seem to pinpoint. Maybe I like my protagonists to be beaten bloody on regular basis. Or maybe I, on some level or other, like dysfunctional relationships. I don't know. I just know that I like how this series wrapped up. So, yeah. Three stars. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Quick question containing a *spoiler*:<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />When did Devlin supposedly rape Opal? Everyone keeps saying Devlin raped Opal but I don't remember that ever happening. Are they referring to the time that he did a soul transfer with Ulrick, so he could seduce Opal? You know, the time they had consensual sex--which, if we're being honest here, wasn't an unpleasant experience for either of them (at the time). If that's what everyone is talking about, and I think it is, I'm going to disagree. He didn't rape her. He deceived her. He tricked her. Lied to her. And, yeah, it was a completely <b>evil</b> a-hole thing to do. But he never raped her. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1165786223298390761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_161801713" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161801713" />
    <a title="Amber" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2676965-amber"><img alt="Amber" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251437648p2/2676965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161801713?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/2676965-amber">Amber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161801713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1151618919592926629">This one was shaping up to be my favourite of Snyder's Glass series, which I haven't been enjoying nearly as much as the Study series. Opal, the main character is just whiny, and never seems to learn from her mistakes. Still I was liking this one. One of my favourite characters from the first book was back, there was plenty of action, and Opal finally seemed to be making some progress towards finding her place in the world and becoming an empowered young woman.<br/><br/>Then in the last 100 pages it just </span>
  <span id="freeText1151618919592926629" style="display:none">This one was shaping up to be my favourite of Snyder's Glass series, which I haven't been enjoying nearly as much as the Study series. Opal, the main character is just whiny, and never seems to learn from her mistakes. Still I was liking this one. One of my favourite characters from the first book was back, there was plenty of action, and Opal finally seemed to be making some progress towards finding her place in the world and becoming an empowered young woman.<br /><br />Then in the last 100 pages it just goes completely off the rails. Sorry, but having to endure two full chapters of male characters rendering Opal powerless and then gleefully describing how they and others are going to rape her is just gross. It's also a complete deviation from the lighter tone and adventurous romp that was the earlier part of the book. Finally having our main character decide at the end of the novel that her true love is a character who tortured her and raped her in the first book of the series, just goes beyond tolerable. Sorry, my memory isn't that short and I don't appreciate the retcon, or that fact that this is portrayed as a happy ending according to Opal, her friends and family. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1151618919592926629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer101820666&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer101820666" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10758823314950036388">My first complaint about the book is the size. I received the book for a birthday present. When sliding it into my book shelf with other Maria Snyder books it is 1/2 inch to an inch taller than the other books. The symmetry throws me off and bothers me.<br/><br/>I have really enjoyed this series until this book. First it majorily dragged on and on. There were a couple of parts that would get exciting and then it would drag some more. The last 140 pages were high paced and exciting. <br/><br/>I loved that Janco, Val</span>
  <span id="freeText10758823314950036388" style="display:none">My first complaint about the book is the size. I received the book for a birthday present. When sliding it into my book shelf with other Maria Snyder books it is 1/2 inch to an inch taller than the other books. The symmetry throws me off and bothers me.<br /><br />I have really enjoyed this series until this book. First it majorily dragged on and on. There were a couple of parts that would get exciting and then it would drag some more. The last 140 pages were high paced and exciting. <br /><br />I loved that Janco, Valek, Ari were in the story. I loved the two little kids and how Opal was with them. <br /><br />The whole Kade thing made me sad. I can understand the problems but I didn't like the way things played out with Opal being unfaithful. If they would have come to a mutual decision before hand than I wouldn't have been bothered. But Kade loved Opal and wanted to be with her and she hurt him.<br /><br />Now my little soap box and I know many other's may have a problem with this as well. I believe in forgiveness and redemption. I believe people can change and become good or bad. I believe we should forgive but we don't have to trust that person again. <br /><br />Is it physically possible to actually feel that way about someone who did all that he was responsible or somewhat responsible for? Maybe if you clinically need medication you can but I doubt someone could go through all she went through with Devlin and be able to love him and want to be married to him. I know there is the whole Stockholm syndrome but technically can people really fall in love with someone who;<br /><br />1) Participated in abducting you so your sister Tula would be murdered<br />2) Tortured you<br />3) Kidnapped you<br />4) Stole someone else's body so he could lead you where he wanted you to go <br />5) Sleep with you while in this other person's body<br />6) Drug you<br />7) Torture a whole lot more<br />8) Manipulates and controls you<br />9) I am sure there is more<br /><br />When did the whole romance actually happen? Because they had only a couple of friendly interactions in book 2 then she only spoke to him a few times in the 3rd book before they are in love and all that. She kissed him only after speaking to him a couple of times. Despite all the reasons listed above Devlen did grow on me. If he would have been a constant in this story some how or at least more a romance, trust and compainionship between the two of them for the last 2 books and a strong relationship building in this book than it may not have bothered me so much. But because of his previous crimes and only a few encounters with each other it doesn't makes sense to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10758823314950036388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer614971541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6194562681000300669">Surely I can't be the only one disgusted by this last book of the series.. If the last book basically was Stockholm Syndrome madeover, then this book was more like a whore addicted to Meth. Yes that sounds harsh, but I don't know how else to describe it. I have liked all of Ms. Snyder's other series, and even found the first in this good, and the second still promising, but this.... Um, WOW! Mind you this just how I feel personally, obviously other people liked the events that took place.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view s</a></span>
  <span id="freeText6194562681000300669" style="display:none">Surely I can't be the only one disgusted by this last book of the series.. If the last book basically was Stockholm Syndrome madeover, then this book was more like a whore addicted to Meth. Yes that sounds harsh, but I don't know how else to describe it. I have liked all of Ms. Snyder's other series, and even found the first in this good, and the second still promising, but this.... Um, WOW! Mind you this just how I feel personally, obviously other people liked the events that took place.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />So we have Opal having been tortured long ago by Devlen in The study series. Then with the first book of this series he tortures her again, not just physically, (although he raped her) but mentally. Then in the second book, she finds a somewhat repentant Devlen and finds she has conflicted feelings her torturer/rapist. And then finally in this book you have a culmination of her sleeping with Devlen while still in a relationship with Kade, getting herself horribly addicted to the blood magic that she spent her whole life fighting against, (Oh and so does Devlen, again, twice)and then of course that leads to her doing disgusting things. DISGUSTING!!<br /><br />If I could get by the fact that she found herself attracted to Devlen, I can't get past the fact that morally (for me) this book is just wrong on so many levels.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The only redeeming qualities of this book is Valek, Yalena, Irys, Janco, Ari, &amp; Leif are prevalent throughout the book. I also ended up being fond of Kade, Nic, &amp; Eve. But where the hell was Zitora? She wasn't in this book at all!<br /><br />I'm sorry Ms. Snyder. I truly am. This should have been an easy knock out for you, (especially since I love your other books), but this one was just bad. Again my opinion. Will it stop me from reading other books Ms. Snyder puts out? Absolutely not, I believe every good author will eventually have a bad book. I just hope that this type of mistake is not repeated.</span>

  <span id="freeText8553190509866045129" style="display:none">Opal has lost her magic.<br /><br />Possibly forever.<br /><br />Though there is a chance she might gain it back if she can retrieve the vials of blood that were stolen from her—stolen and hidden by three men locked in a high security prison.<br /><br />Unfortunately that prison is so secure even the Councilors of Ixia can’t obtain legal entrance.<br /><br />Which just means Opal will have to find another way. But will that way require selling her soul to addiction? Or to the man who once tortured her? Or to the Commander’s assassin?<br /><br />So many options. And Opal really only needs one.<br /><br />Ooh, I liked this book! My favorite of Snyder’s Glass series. It didn’t lead where I expected. Or where I hoped it would at the beginning of the novel. But it was full of suspense. And Opal finally grew a backbone. Though my FAVORITE part was watching her deal with her mother’s fury after Opal showed up late for her sister’s wedding. LOL.<br /><br />Important Note: This is the third book in the Glass series, but actually the 6th book set in this world with these characters. The Study series comes first. Begin with POISON STUDY. You will not be sorry. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1625501869" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5647142605030982290">Okay, I'm not going to write a full review here, but there is ONE HUGE issue I want to discuss.<br/><br/>In the last book, there was a hint of a love triangle between Delven, Kade, and Opal, so I'm sure you're all expecting one in this book.<br/><br/>Well, ding ding ding ding!<br/><br/>I won't tell you who she chooses or anything like that, but let me tell you something:<br/><br/>I accepted Delven's whole wanting to redeem himself thing, and wanting to help out, and even falling in love with Opal. I even, reluctantly, accepted that sh</span>
  <span id="freeText5647142605030982290" style="display:none">Okay, I'm not going to write a full review here, but there is ONE HUGE issue I want to discuss.<br /><br />In the last book, there was a hint of a love triangle between Delven, Kade, and Opal, so I'm sure you're all expecting one in this book.<br /><br />Well, ding ding ding ding!<br /><br />I won't tell you who she chooses or anything like that, but let me tell you something:<br /><br />I accepted Delven's whole wanting to redeem himself thing, and wanting to help out, and even falling in love with Opal. I even, reluctantly, accepted that she may have been confused about him because of all the TORTURE and sweet talk and everything he had done to her.<br /><br />HOWEVER! I do NOT accept the fact that he was even remotely in the running for her affections, HELLO! He TORTURED her for weeks! TWICE! He lied to her and used her and kidnapped her and did I mention tortured?<br /><br />Forgive him and all, because that's always good for the heart, but saying that it's acceptable to basically say that all of his deeds were nothing, is wrong.<br /><br />The author did NOT represent trauma correctly at all. Especially because it took almost nothing at all for Opal to forgive him and stop being scared of him.<br /><br />Sorry, no.<br /><br />PS: two stars instead of one because there were certain parts of the book I did enjoy. But again: sorry, but no.</span>

<div id="review_95354984" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95354984" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2691297-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331223010p2/2691297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95354984?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/2691297-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780778328476" href="/book/show/7698740-spy-glass">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2691297-julie?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95354984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9639505107225713218">After reading the first two books in this series, I felt pretty confident that I knew where the story was headed. And while I was reading “Spy Glass”, Maria V. Snyder’s third and final installment in her Glass’ series, I realized one thing: Boy, I didn’t know nothin’!<br/><br/>What a ride! From beginning to end, I was rendered speechless. If I was a nail biter, I would have chewed them all!<br/><br/>Opal is trying her hardest to deal with the aftermath of what happened at the end of “Sea Glass”. And who comes to he</span>
  <span id="freeText9639505107225713218" style="display:none">After reading the first two books in this series, I felt pretty confident that I knew where the story was headed. And while I was reading “Spy Glass”, Maria V. Snyder’s third and final installment in her Glass’ series, I realized one thing: Boy, I didn’t know nothin’!<br /><br />What a ride! From beginning to end, I was rendered speechless. If I was a nail biter, I would have chewed them all!<br /><br />Opal is trying her hardest to deal with the aftermath of what happened at the end of “Sea Glass”. And who comes to her aid? Valek! Yup, Valek from Maria’s ‘Study’ series makes an appearance in the first chapter! I had forgotten how much I love that character. Okay, I’m full of it. How can one forget why they love Valek? What I mean is that this book has reminded me why Valek is on my favorite characters list and why he was my first literary crush. He’s funny and smart and sexy and dangerous and…*sigh* What was I saying? Oh yeah. *clears throat* Valek trains Opal so she can become a kick ass heroine and break into Fulgor’s maximum security prison. At least that’s the plan.<br /><br />Maria visited a prison to research her role, and as with every other time she has put research into something for her writing, you can really tell. The particulars she includes in Opal’s visits to the prison in Fulgor are incredibly detailed and accurate.<br /><br />The last few chapters are filled with gut-wrenching suspense. My brain was telling me not to fret too much because of course Opal will come out fine at the end…but my gut was not listening! The last section of the book is filled with twists like you would not believe. Also, the last few chapters remind you that this is NOT a YA title! There are some pretty graphic scenes and some pretty mature themes going on there! A true testament to Opal’s character is how strong she remains through it all and how she keeps her wits about her. She can still put her needs aside to lend a hand and try to save the masses.<br /><br />In this installment, there are two characters who are actively trying to win Opal’s heart. Kade and Devlen. Yup, Devlen. And after following these lovely characters through three books, I feel one of them just makes sense. He wants what’s best for Opal. He reminds her of her worth and doesn’t care whether or not she regains all that she’s lost. He makes her happy, and isn’t that the most important part?<br /><br />In the end, “Spy Glass” did not disappoint me at all. As a third and final installment in a series, it answered all my questions and left a hopeful future for our heroine that I’ve been rooting for for so long. “Spy Glass” did not end the way I had anticipated, but had a great ending none the less. I am very happy with how the series concluded. Opal is content. She is happy with her place in the world, with her family and with her husband. Yup, I said husband. If you’ve read the first two books, I guarantee that you’ll love this one! Those who are new to this trilogy and who are fans of action / adventure fantasy novels, these books will keep your interest long enough for you to wish for more. Maria does it again. Now we just have to wait until her next unique and interesting title come to the bookstore – and hopefully one day we’ll see another series set in the world we’ve grown to love over 6 books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9639505107225713218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22195799-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514812938p2/22195799.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1335072937?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/22195799-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18965591-spy-glass">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1335072937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15441271086795529707">I read this series to help with a book hangover I received from reading a different series and it definitely helped! However, now I have another book hangover from this amazing series so what do I read now??<br/><br/>Opal has been through so many terrible things since the beginning of this series. She has been kidnapped several times, tortured, harassed, accused of terrible things, arrested and imprisoned as well. She has been betrayed or tricked by almost every male character is this book series. She has</span>
  <span id="freeText15441271086795529707" style="display:none">I read this series to help with a book hangover I received from reading a different series and it definitely helped! However, now I have another book hangover from this amazing series so what do I read now??<br /><br />Opal has been through so many terrible things since the beginning of this series. She has been kidnapped several times, tortured, harassed, accused of terrible things, arrested and imprisoned as well. She has been betrayed or tricked by almost every male character is this book series. She has the worst luck with men. I'm happy that she finally found her happy ending with a wonderful man (whom I won't mention by name but I have a serious crush on him now). I always got so angry when anyone messed with her and because of her astounding record of getting into trouble, it was a rollercoaster of emotions. <br /><br />I had a trouble staying with Opal's romances because I knew who she was going to end up with. I was skeptical at first but I couldn't be happier for her. She has really grown from the first book. She is more confident and has found who she really is. She no longer allows herself to be haunted by past events and she can see clearly. She blamed herself for a lot of things she couldn't control but she has matured greatly and has accepted her past mistakes and decisions. I never thought I could love another character as much as I love Yelena but Opal has won a place in my heart. <br /><br />Maria V. Snyder has created another amazing series.This entire series was so fast paced I blazed right threw these three books. I can't believe it is over. I read the first three Study books then read Shadow Study so some things were definitely missing as the Glass series fits right between the two. Everything fits nicely now and I can't wait to read the rest of the Study series. <br /><br />Overall: 5 stars<br />Recommendation: Yes. If you love the first two Glass books then just keep on going to this finale.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_308097272" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308097272" />
    <a title="Caitlin Thomson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8640762-caitlin-thomson"><img alt="Caitlin Thomson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438175414p2/8640762.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308097272?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin Thomson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin Thomson" href="/user/show/8640762-caitlin-thomson">Caitlin Thomson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer308097272&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308097272" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10485457768702121042">I loved this series as a whole, and seriously enjoy Snyder's fresh approaches to the worlds of magic. This book, however, was seriously disappointing.<br/>Some characters are mysteriously absent, others act out of character and (even worse) sub plots concerning these characters are left hanging forever.<br/>The plot is poorly paced, with all the events relevant to the ending happening in the last chapters with everything else up to this point being forgotten.<br/>I was almost enjoying this book until I realise</span>
  <span id="freeText10485457768702121042" style="display:none">I loved this series as a whole, and seriously enjoy Snyder's fresh approaches to the worlds of magic. This book, however, was seriously disappointing.<br />Some characters are mysteriously absent, others act out of character and (even worse) sub plots concerning these characters are left hanging forever.<br />The plot is poorly paced, with all the events relevant to the ending happening in the last chapters with everything else up to this point being forgotten.<br />I was almost enjoying this book until I realised that the plot was on a one way track - I could understand Devlin earning some redemption (bug not trust) from Opal as part of her healing process, and he could have been a sympathetic second love interest which ultimately strengthened the main couple (a believable possible development around Chapter 15). <br />This would have been clever, pulling at the reader's heart strings but acknowledging the disbelief that Opal would suddenly claim to be in love with him while never ending her relationship with Kade, especially considering her past involvements with Devlin and her trust issues.<br />Part of me hopes that there was originally a fully developed plot to explain these holes (possible, as Opal and Kade breaking up had been hinted at in the second book) and I'm sure that THAT story would have been more believable. This one just reads as a last minute attempt to further ruin the heroine's life.<br />Opal started off the series likeable (if overly naïve) and ended up almost hate-worthy. All her problems went from being from the outside (the Council's manipulation and Devlin) to of her own creation. <br />Overall, this book is like watching a train-wreck that sometimes stops at random stations but leaves before it can be repaired. Riddled with plot-holes and inconsistencies, this is not the ending that I was expecting for this series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10485457768702121042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1522149947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1522149947" />
    <a title="Siobhan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan"><img alt="Siobhan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510311895p2/35855553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1522149947?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siobhan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siobhan" href="/user/show/35855553-siobhan">Siobhan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20444001-spy-glass">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1522149947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5587295961937362640">A great end to the Glass series.<br/><br/>Throughout the first two books I was somewhat annoyed by how prominent the romantic aspects of the story happened to be, especially after the Study series was kind enough not to force multiple love triangles into the story. However, in this book I was quite surprised by the twists and turns thrown into the romantic aspect. I admit, I did not enjoy the twists, but they were somewhat unexpected. Fortunately, as I was not as engrossed in the romantic aspects as I was</span>
  <span id="freeText5587295961937362640" style="display:none">A great end to the Glass series.<br /><br />Throughout the first two books I was somewhat annoyed by how prominent the romantic aspects of the story happened to be, especially after the Study series was kind enough not to force multiple love triangles into the story. However, in this book I was quite surprised by the twists and turns thrown into the romantic aspect. I admit, I did not enjoy the twists, but they were somewhat unexpected. Fortunately, as I was not as engrossed in the romantic aspects as I was the fantasy aspect, such a thing didn’t bother me as much as it could have.<br /><br />For me, what I particularly loved about this book was the reappearance of characters from the Study series. Most importantly, is the reappearance of Valek. In my opinion, he has never really been as well developed as the other characters – yet in this one things seem to change. He actually becomes a real person this time, rather than the individual with a faux air of mystique. It was nice to see some development for his character, considering how I had hoped for it during the Study series.<br /><br />In terms of the actual storyline, this one brings the Glass series to a nice ending. As with the Study series, things are brought together well – giving us the answers to the questions we had left in our minds. Yet, at the same time, it leaves us interested to see what else is in store for Ixia.<br /><br />In short, I cannot wait to get my hands on my next Ixia read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5587295961937362640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4768659156978235916">Damsel-in-Distress Call, Repeat. Damsel-in-Distress Call, Please Send Valek, Ari & Janco As Soon As Possible, Oh and Maybe Yelena too Just for Good Measure<br/>Spy Glass<br/>Rating: 5/5<br/><br/>Summary: Opal has sacrificed her powers to end blood magic, or so she thought. Turns out, while she was being held captive, Tricky & Ulrick kept some of her blood and now it may be out there just waiting for someone else to use it. But what if Opal reclaims it? Will she get her powers back? After spending time moping, Opal </span>
  <span id="freeText4768659156978235916" style="display:none">Damsel-in-Distress Call, Repeat. Damsel-in-Distress Call, Please Send Valek, Ari &amp; Janco As Soon As Possible, Oh and Maybe Yelena too Just for Good Measure<br />Spy Glass<br />Rating: 5/5<br /><br />Summary: Opal has sacrificed her powers to end blood magic, or so she thought. Turns out, while she was being held captive, Tricky &amp; Ulrick kept some of her blood and now it may be out there just waiting for someone else to use it. But what if Opal reclaims it? Will she get her powers back? After spending time moping, Opal decides to do something, she’s going to find her blood which means she needs to talk to Ulrick. But the only problem with that is he’s in maximum security Wirral prison in Fulgor.<br /><br />This book was my favorite, no contest. Opal has no doubts about her abilities. She has no magic, so she has no choice but to rely on her immunity and fighting skills (&amp; Quartz). Her confidence has grown by miles since Storm Glass, she truly is a different person. Gosh, it’s so hard to write a coherent review because I just want to like laugh and cry and point at things and flail and scream cause THIS BOOK. UGH it was just so great. I will try to be coherent for your sake.<br /><br />Okay so the romance. I’VE SWITCHED TEAMS I’M NOT SORRY. Devlen is just yes. I could tell in Storm Glass that he totally had a thing for Opal, but in Sea Glass after his addiction for magic was gone, I knew he had changed for good. Though it took our girl Opal here a while to figure that one out. I knew they would be together when it was Devlen Opal kept turning to with her problems. I gotta say there’s something about Devlen that’s alluring for sure. Besides the blue eyes and muscles, there’s something about his personality that I could feel. The way Snyder describes how he talks and moves, I don’t know, it’s like almost lyrical, and enticing. But I still love Kade too, but Opal &amp; Devlen belong together, it broke my heart when Kade accepted it so completely. He’s too sweet for this world. <br /><br />The plot was very captivating! There’s always something happening. I thought Snyder was pulling something on me when Finn was introduced and Opal went on a fake date, but he wasn’t a love interest at all thank god. I was like no. There’s already too much drama there, thank you very much. Valek was also in this book more since Opal is immune to magic just like him. He teaches her how to be a sneak and I very much enjoyed that part of the book. Snyder has a way of making long time spans pass very quickly but realistically which was awesome because spy training 101 takes a while. <br /><br />I was sad that Zitora didn’t come back into this. I was hoping for more of a parallel of Irys/Yelena with Opal &amp; Zitora. It happened in Storm Glass but kind of fell apart in Sea Glass and then she took off. I wonder if she’ll get her own spin off series while looking for her sister. That would be epic. DUDES, Opal gets to talk to her horse in this book!!! You should read it for that reason alone if nothing else. Horse talk is the best. I miss Kiki, and with that I’m going to read Shadow Study, peace.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7598135008363040314">I am disappointed with the last volume in the glass series. Not that I think she should have been with Kade but falling in love with someone who tortured her and caused emotional pain is masochistic. It sounded almost too contrived. Hello trust issues? Two conversations with the Devlen flips her feelings? <br/><br/>I also felt like she tried to jam too many characters into her last volume. Janco got lots of line time but Ari was only there to help advance the story. Was it the last kick at the bucket for </span>
  <span id="freeText7598135008363040314" style="display:none">I am disappointed with the last volume in the glass series. Not that I think she should have been with Kade but falling in love with someone who tortured her and caused emotional pain is masochistic. It sounded almost too contrived. Hello trust issues? Two conversations with the Devlen flips her feelings? <br /><br />I also felt like she tried to jam too many characters into her last volume. Janco got lots of line time but Ari was only there to help advance the story. Was it the last kick at the bucket for all of her characters before the story ended except Yelena? I am all for returning characters, in fact I love it. Yet, it felt off and why would everyone drop everything for Opal and come to her rescue? I understand loyalty but all of these people hold different positions and responsibilities. To drop all of that and come from various places to help a friend is noble and incredibly nice but I feel like in the realm of possibilities that the chance of getting ALL of them is slim to none. A comment or two about a character being held back would have been cool. but nothing. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oSAWLZmJMrEFRN8TsdfLR0J3nxytY9yEcALSwrqpV3iAPFer/TxwNK6hgQq2RiucWVypXwwJOF+co/aOlEoCNg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4585628166451004299">When Maria V. Snyder was younger, she aspired to be a storm chaser in the American Midwest so she attended Pennsylvania State University and earned a Bachelor of Science degree in Meteorology. Much to her chagrin, forecasting the weather wasn’t in her skill set so she spent a number of years as an environmental meteorologist, which is not exciting...at all. Bored at work and needing a creative out</span>
  <span id="freeText4585628166451004299" style="display:none">When Maria V. Snyder was younger, she aspired to be a storm chaser in the American Midwest so she attended Pennsylvania State University and earned a Bachelor of Science degree in Meteorology. Much to her chagrin, forecasting the weather wasn’t in her skill set so she spent a number of years as an environmental meteorologist, which is not exciting...at all. Bored at work and needing a creative outlet, she started writing fantasy and science fiction stories. Over twenty novels and numerous short stories later, Maria’s learned a thing or three about writing. She’s been on the New York Times bestseller list, won a dozen awards, and has earned her Masters of Arts degree in Writing from Seton Hill University, where she is now a faculty member. Her favorite color is red. She loves dogs, but is allergic, instead she has a big black tom cat named…Kitty (apparently naming cats isn’t in her skill set either). Maria also has a husband and two children who are an inspiration for her writing when they aren't being a distraction. Note: She mentions her cat before her family. <br /><br />When she's not writing she's either playing volleyball, traveling, or taking pictures. Being a writer, though is a ton of fun. Where else can you take fencing lessons, learn how to ride a horse, study marital arts, learn how to pick a lock, take glass blowing classes and attend Astronomy Camp and call it research? Maria will be the first one to tell you it's not working as a meteorologist.<br /><br />Readers are welcome to check out her website for book excerpts, free short stories, maps, blog, and her schedule at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.MariaVSnyder.com">http://www.MariaVSnyder.com</a>.</span>
